**Cognitive style, evolving:** in this period she would have completed the cognitive work that the published record reveals her as having *already done* by 2014 — the construction of a workable, durable map of which American things were dangerous (loose mixing of unrelated youth; drift from prayer; food provenance; the wrong kinds of friends) and which were neutral or good (public schools, libraries, certain neighbors, civic life, NPR in the kitchen). The map is *specific*, not paranoid — a key marker. Paranoid acculturation produces blanket prohibition; Muneeba's prohibitions are itemized. This itemization is the cognitive fingerprint of someone who *worked the problem* rather than retreating from it.

**Self-concept, evolving:** consolidated around competence-under-conditions-of-displacement. Berry's acculturation typology places her firmly in the *integration* quadrant (high maintenance of heritage culture, high engagement with host culture) — not *separation* (which would have produced an enclave-only existence) and not *assimilation* (which would have produced abandonment of hijab, of Urdu in the home, of the masjid). Integration is the most psychologically demanding of Berry's four positions; it requires holding two cultural grammars simultaneously and choosing between them constantly. That she occupies it with apparent equanimity by the time of canonical entry suggests the integration work was *completed* in this decade.

**Attachment, evolving:** the marriage to Yusuf, depicted across the run as affectionate, equitable, and tender (the hand-holding during Yusuf's cardiac scare; the shared private jokes in Urdu; the unforced physical comfort), is the *earned-secure* relationship that recalibrated whatever insecurities the upheaval of emigration produced. By the end of this decade she is, in attachment terms, partnered-secure with a working internal model of "I am held; I hold others."

---

## III. ESTABLISHED MOTHERHOOD — 1990s through EARLY 2010s (Muneeba aged roughly 30–45, Aamir's childhood and Kamala's pre-adolescence)

Canonical evidence: family photographs and flashback panels in *Ms. Marvel* (2014) showing a younger Muneeba with young Kamala — visibly warmer, more physically affectionate, *laughing* in a register the present-day character rarely accesses publicly.

**Affect regulation, this era:** *highest expressed warmth of her published life*. The flashback evidence is unambiguous — she is shown holding small Kamala, reading to her, laughing at her, dressing her up. The dry, contained adult register is *not yet operational* as the dominant mode. This is critical to the longitudinal picture: Muneeba was not always the Wall. The Wall was *built*, and built in response to *something*. The likeliest something — derivable from the canonical timing — is Kamala's approach to adolescence, the gender-asymmetric tightening that begins as a daughter becomes a *young woman* in a diaspora context. Aamir, as a son, did not trigger this re-engineering; Kamala did, because the cultural stakes of a daughter's adolescence (marriageability, reputation, *izzat*) are categorically higher in the operative cultural frame.

**Cognitive style, this era:** *expanded and synthesizing*. This is the period in which she would have absorbed American parenting inputs (the pediatrician's vocabulary, the school's parent-teacher conferences, the other mothers at the bus stop) and metabolized them into a hybrid operating system. The evidence of this synthesis is her later fluency in *both* registers — she can deploy "what will Auntie Ruby say" *and* "your grades are slipping" with equal naturalness. Most first-generation parents become fluent in only one of those vocabularies; she is fluent in both.

**Self-concept, this era:** Eriksonian *Generativity* in full bloom. Her self-worth is fully invested in the production and shaping of the next generation — Aamir's faith formation, Kamala's character formation, the household's cultural transmission. This is the developmental peak of her life as canon depicts it; everything before was preparation, everything after will be defense and revision of what was built here.

**Embryonic anxious overlay:** the hypervigilance toward Kamala specifically — gendered, targeted, persistent — likely *originates* in the late part of this era, as Kamala enters middle school, begins to come home with American-specific social problems (the social hierarchies at Coles Academic, the boy-girl mixing, the food anxieties of being the brown-bag-lunch kid), and Muneeba realizes the maps she built in Era II are inadequate to the adolescent terrain. The tightening begins not from cruelty or anxiety-disorder but from *map insufficiency*.

---

## IV. THE WALL ERA — c. 2013–2015 (Muneeba aged roughly 45–47, Kamala 16)

This is where canonical observation begins. The Muneeba of *Ms. Marvel* #1 is the Muneeba of *peak gendered enforcement*: maximum surveillance, maximum cold-withdrawal-as-discipline, minimum expressed warmth toward Kamala in the public family register.

**Affect regulation, this era:** *aggressive deployment of suppression in service of role*. She is not feeling less; she is showing less, deliberately. The evidence that this is performance-of-role rather than affective constriction proper is found in the *Last Days* arc (#16–19) only months later, in which the role drops *instantly* under genuine threat — the tenderness underneath was not absent, only suspended. Linehan's framework is useful here: Muneeba is not affect-dysregulated; she is *over-regulated* in a context-specific way, and the over-regulation is *strategic*, not symptomatic.

**Cognitive style, this era:** *narrower than her actual range*. She is operating, with Kamala, on simplified rule-enforcement protocols that do not reflect her full cognitive capacity. This is a known parental phenomenon — the simplification of one's own complexity for the perceived pedagogical needs of an adolescent. Whether this was wise is debatable in canon (Kamala experiences it as suffocating); whether it was *characterological* is not. It was a *deployed* style, not her trait style.

**Self-concept, this era:** *strained*. The Era III generative self is encountering its first major resistance — Kamala is not absorbing the transmission cleanly, is lying, is sneaking out, is — unbeknownst to Kamala but, as the record will reveal, *not unbeknownst to Muneeba* — also engaged in costumed superheroism. The self-concept survives by *narrowing*: she retreats from "shaper of children" to "enforcer of minimum standards." The narrowing protects the self-concept from confronting the possibility of failed transmission.

**Critical observation — the perception that was not yet disclosed:** by mid-2015, Muneeba *already knows* Kamala is Ms. Marvel. The revelation comes in #19, but the language ("for a long time") establishes that the knowing predates the disclosure by months at minimum. This means the Wall Era's surveillance behavior must be re-read: she was not merely enforcing curfews to enforce curfews; she was *holding the shape of normal life* around a daughter she knew was carrying something unbearable. This is a *highly sophisticated* affective and cognitive operation, and the file should register it as such. She chose to be experienced as the antagonist of her daughter's adolescence in order to provide her daughter with the only stable structure that adolescence had. Few parents could execute that.

---

## V. THE CRACK AND THE REVELATION — 2015–2017 (Muneeba aged roughly 47–49)

**Affect regulation, this era:** *the role-suspension capacity is canonically established*. Under the Incursion-scale threat of *Last Days*, the disciplinary register is set down without struggle, and the underlying tenderness is shown to be *fully accessible* — she prays with Kamala, holds her, does not lecture. The clinical significance: her over-regulation is *not* an inability to access feeling; it is a *deployed* organization of feeling that can be reorganized at will when conditions demand. This is the marker of *mature ego function* in the Vaillant sense.

The revelation in #19 — "I have known for a long time. I am proud of you. I will not ask you to stop." — is the *single most important behavioral data point in her entire file*, because it demonstrates four capacities simultaneously: (1) accurate perception sustained over time without disclosure, (2) tolerance for the anxiety of that perception without symptomatic discharge, (3) capacity to revise the parenting model when revision becomes appropriate, (4) capacity to extend rather than withdraw permission in response to evidence of a child's competence. The combination is rare.

**Cognitive style, this era:** *expansion and re-integration*. The narrowing of the Wall Era reverses. She returns to her fuller cognitive range, now with the additional integration that her daughter is, in fact, a hero — a fact she folds into her operating worldview without apparent crisis. The religious framework absorbs the superhero fact (Allah's plan; the obligations of the gifted; *fard kifaya* — the communal obligation that some must take up so that all are protected) without strain. This is *intellectualization in its mature form* — the religious vocabulary giving her a container for an otherwise incomprehensible reality.

**Self-concept, this era:** *reorganized upward*. From "enforcer of minimum standards" she moves to "mother of a hero" — but the published evidence is that she does not *advertise* this self-concept; she holds it privately, with Yusuf, in the household. The self-concept revision is internal, not performative. The community register stays unchanged. This is significant: many parents experiencing a comparable revision would *broadcast*, would shift their public self-presentation. Muneeba does not. Her self-concept is independent of external validation, as Section 3 of the workup noted, and this era confirms it operationally.

---

## VI. INTEGRATION ERA — 2017–2021 (Muneeba aged roughly 49–53)

The Ahmed run and the surrounding material give us the *post-revelation steady state*: a Muneeba whose parenting has matured into ally-with-residual-vigilance, whose marriage is tested by Yusuf's cardiac event and survives strengthened, whose extended family expands with Aamir's marriage to Tyesha.

**Affect regulation, this era:** *stable, range-expanded, but tested*. Yusuf's cardiac scare introduces the first canonical encounter with a threat to her *peer attachment* (as opposed to her child-attachment). The behavioral response is diagnostic: she takes over the logistical and medical labor without complaint, manages his medication and diet, *shields Kamala from the full severity of the prognosis*, and processes her own fear in private — likely in prayer, likely with one or two Aunties, almost certainly not with her children. The pattern is *continuous with her lifelong style* and gives no evidence of decompensation. The over-regulation here serves its proper function: protecting dependents from a fear that would not help them.

**Cognitive style, this era:** *most flexible of her recorded life*. The Tyesha integration is the case study. Initial coolness (a Black American convert is not what she had pictured for Aamir; the cultural distance is real; the community-gossip register is loud) gives way, observably, to genuine acceptance once *evidence* of Tyesha's sincerity, character, and commitment accumulates. This is Bayesian parenting in operation — prior beliefs held *until* evidence warrants update, then updated cleanly without resentment. The same mechanism is visible in her processing of Aamir's deeper religiosity (which she had initially treated with mild exasperation) and of Kamala's heroism.

**Self-concept, this era:** *expanded toward elder-stateswoman of the household*. She is becoming the *matriarch* — not yet grandmother, but the woman to whom the next generation (Tyesha included) defers, the woman who decides when the family gathers, what is served, what is said. Erikson's transition from generativity toward integrity is beginning, though not complete.

---

## VII. THE LOSS — 2022–2023 (Muneeba aged roughly 54–55)

The death of Kamala in *The Death of Ms. Marvel* and the surrounding material constitutes the *peak adverse event* of her file.

**Affect regulation, this era:** *the lifelong containment strategy is stress-tested at maximum load and holds*. The grief is depicted as nearly mute in public, devastating in private — the *exact* signature one would predict from the longitudinal record. She does not collapse, does not somatize, does not develop substance use, does not withdraw from her surviving family. She continues to function. The public-private split that has been her affective architecture since the late 1980s does the work it was built for.

The clinical question this era forces is whether the containment is *healthy* or merely *successful*. The published evidence — that she continues to engage meaningfully with Yusuf, with Aamir, with the community, that she retains affective range with intimates, that the grief is *integrated* into religious practice rather than walled off from it — argues for the former. Bonanno's resilience research is directly applicable: a substantial subset of bereaved adults (perhaps a third to a half) show the *resilience trajectory* he documents — acute distress followed by sustained functional preservation without pathology. Muneeba is canonically that subset.

**Cognitive style, this era:** *narrowed to essentials, religiously scaffolded*. The full intellectual range she displayed in Era VI contracts somewhat — she is operating, in the grief period, on the core operating system (prayer, household, the people in front of her). This is adaptive, not regressive. The religious framework provides the meaning-architecture (Allah's plan; the *shaheed* status of one who dies in righteous action; the certainty of reunion) that allows grief to be *bearable* rather than *meaningful-less*. Park's meaning-making model in bereavement is directly relevant — Muneeba's pre-loss meaning system was robust enough to *absorb* the loss without requiring fundamental reconstruction. Most parents who lose a child experience the opposite: the pre-loss meaning system shatters and must be rebuilt from scratch, a process that takes years and that many do not complete. Muneeba's system absorbed.

**Self-concept, this era:** *threatened but preserved*. The generative self-concept — "mother of these children" — sustains its most serious challenge. The preservation mechanism is the religious reframe (she is still Kamala's mother; the relationship is suspended, not ended) and the continued presence of Aamir, Tyesha, and the eventual grandchild. The self-concept does not collapse; it *re-centers* around the surviving relationships and the spiritual continuity.

---

## VIII. RESURRECTION AND MUTANT REVEAL — 2023 onward (Muneeba aged 55+)

The posthumous mutant reveal and the X-Men resurrection (*Ms. Marvel: The New Mutant* material) deliver to Muneeba a sequence that would destabilize most subjects: her daughter is dead; her daughter is revealed to have been a mutant (an identity category that, in the Marvel universe, carries its own freight of stigma and danger Muneeba had not been parenting around); her daughter is alive again.

**Affect regulation, this era:** *the established pattern holds, on accelerated timeline*. The revelation-acceptance-worry sequence that took years across the original Ms. Marvel disclosure compresses, in the mutant reveal, to a much shorter cycle. The internal mechanism is the same — perceive, contain, update, accept, continue to worry within the updated frame. The acceleration suggests the *capacity for revision* is now well-rehearsed; she has done this before, and the muscle memory is operational.

**Cognitive style, this era:** *fully integrative*. The mutant category is folded into the operating system alongside the superhero category, the heroic-death category, the resurrection category, with the religious framework continuing to do its containing work. The cognitive operation here is non-trivial — most operating systems, religious or secular, would strain under the resurrection alone. Hers does not visibly strain. The reason, traceable through the longitudinal record, is that her religious framework was *never literalist-fragile*; it was always *meaning-elastic*, organized around principles (Allah's mercy, Allah's plan, the obligation to be grateful) that scale to accommodate unusual data.

**Self-concept, this era:** *moving toward Eriksonian integrity*. The Era VI matriarch is, in this era, becoming the *elder* — the woman whose function in the family is increasingly to *bear witness*, to hold continuity across generations, to be the keeper of the story of who they have been. The self-concept is no longer organized around shaping; it is organized around *holding*. This is the developmentally appropriate movement for her age and her circumstances, and the published record shows it occurring cleanly.

---

## IX. CROSS-DECADE SYNTHESIS — WHAT EVOLVED, WHAT DID NOT

**What did not evolve (trait-level constants across the entire record):**

- The mature suppression defense — present from at least Era II, operational continuously through Era VIII.
- The secure attachment baseline — present from at least Era II (with Yusuf), generalized to children, generalized to community.
- The Bayesian revisability — present in latent form from Era I, operational across every major revision the record documents.
- The independence of self-concept from external validation — visible in every era; she has never been canonically depicted as needing to be *seen* in order to know who she is.
- The religious framework as integrative container — present from Era I, load-bearing across every subsequent era including the maximum-load grief era.

**What evolved (state-level and role-level changes):**

- Expressed warmth toward Kamala — high in Era III, suppressed in Era IV, restored in Era V and after.
- Breadth of cognitive range deployed in parenting — narrowed in Era IV, expanded in Era V onward.
- Self-concept emphasis — shaper (Era III) → enforcer (Era IV) → ally (Era V–VI) → matriarch (Era VI–VII) → elder/witness (Era VIII).
- Acculturation map sophistication — built in Era II, refined in Era III, *adequately adapted to adolescence* only by Era V, after the Wall Era's map-insufficiency had been acknowledged.
- Public-private affective ratio — relatively balanced in early American years, sharply split during Wall Era, re-balanced post-revelation.

**The longitudinal verdict:** Muneeba Khan's psychology has been, across the full canonical sweep, *structurally stable and tactically adaptive*. The architecture (secure attachment, mature suppression, religiously-scaffolded meaning system, role-organized self-concept) was built in the first three decades of her life and has neither failed nor required reconstruction across the subsequent three. What has changed is *which room of that architecture she is living in* at any given era — the architecture itself has held under acculturation, under adolescence, under cardiac scare, under bereavement, and under resurrection. There are not many subjects in the file whose architecture would.

*End Section 3.B. Continue to Section 3.C — Defensive Structure and Compensatory Mechanisms.*


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — SUBJECT: MUNEEBA KHAN

*File Section 04. Diagnostic synthesis built on Stage-One behavioral workup. All assessments derived from longitudinal behavioral evidence in canonical record (Wilson 2014–2019; Ahmed 2019–2021; bereavement and resurrection arcs 2022–present). Subject has no documented psychiatric history of record — i.e., no depicted treatment contact, no medication, no hospitalization, no clinician-of-record across roughly a decade of published material. This absence is itself diagnostically informative and will be treated as such, not as a gap.*

---

## 4.1 Headline Determination

**No Axis I disorder, no Axis II disorder, no substance-use disorder, no trauma- or stressor-related disorder reaches diagnostic threshold on the available record.**

This is an unusually clean finding for a subject of this age cohort (mid-to-late 40s in early canon, early 50s by the bereavement arc), of this migration profile (first-generation South Asian immigrant to the U.S. Northeast corridor, almost certainly arriving as a young adult), and of this exposure profile (mother of a superhuman child living through two Incursion-level extinction events, a citywide super-villain occupation of her hometown, her husband's coronary event, her daughter's death, and her daughter's resurrection on a sovereign mutant nation-state). Most subjects with comparable stressor loads accumulate at least subclinical PTSD features, depressive episodes, or somatoform symptoms. Muneeba does not.

The clean diagnostic ledger is not because the file is thin — the file is, by superhuman-relative civilian standards, dense. It is because her observed coping architecture is *unusually well-matched to her stressor topology*. This match is the central psychiatric finding of this section, and the differential below is organized around defending it against the disorders it most superficially resembles.

---

## 4.2 What IS Clinically Present (Sub-Diagnostic)

Three sub-threshold presentations recur in the record and warrant naming, because each could be mistaken — by a clinician working from a single snapshot — for a frank disorder.

### 4.2.1 Trait-level Constricted Affect with Intact Range

Muneeba's modal facial and vocal register, across writers, is *narrow*. She does not laugh loudly, does not raise her voice except under provocation of moral seriousness, does not weep in front of non-mahram persons, does not display elation, does not display rage. The narrowness is consistent enough that a naive observer would code it as flat affect.

It is not flat affect. The range is intact and accessible; what is constricted is the *aperture* she opens in public. Inside the home, with Yusuf, with Kamala under duress, with Aamir on his wedding day, she demonstrates the full normal-range repertoire — tenderness, joy, fear, anger, humor (the dry register noted in §3). The constriction is therefore behavioral norm-following, not anhedonic blunting. Schizotypal, schizoid, and negative-symptom-spectrum considerations fail at the first step on this basis.

### 4.2.2 Hypervigilance, Targeted and Proportionate

Muneeba scans. She tracks Kamala's whereabouts, phone, friends, clothing, and food intake; she scans the masjid social field for emerging gossip vectors; she monitors Yusuf's color and breathing post-cardiac-event; she registers strangers at the door before Yusuf does. This is the surface phenomenology of an anxiety disorder.

It is not an anxiety disorder. The hypervigilance is (a) *content-specific* — bounded to her recognized domains of responsibility, not generalized to non-relevant stimuli; (b) *evidence-calibrated* — when she learns Kamala is Ms. Marvel, the monitoring intensity does not increase, because she had already correctly inferred most of what she had previously been worried about; (c) *non-impairing* — she sleeps, eats, executes household and community functions; (d) *non-distressing in the ego-dystonic sense* — she experiences her vigilance as a duty of office, not as intrusive worry she would prefer to be rid of.

This is *parental-role hypervigilance in a high-threat acculturation context*, which the comparative clinical literature (Suárez-Orozco; Falicov; the Karachi-diaspora ethnographies) treats as normative-adaptive, not pathological.

### 4.2.3 Suppression-Dominant Affect Regulation

Across every catastrophic beat in the record — the Incursion, the cardiac event, the death of her daughter, the resurrection — Muneeba's first move is the same: visible composure, private processing, delayed release in religious or domestic ritual context. This is not denial (immature defense) and not repression (unconscious exclusion). It is *suppression* — a mature defense in the Vaillant taxonomy — and it is the spine of her clinical picture.

The risk profile of suppression-dominance is well known: under sufficient and sustained load, it can decompensate into somatization, complicated grief, or a late-life depressive episode. The record contains no evidence of this decompensation through the most recent material, but the dossier flags it as the most plausible future failure mode, and §4.6 (Course) returns to it.

---

## 4.3 Etiology — Where the Picture Comes From

The convergent pressures shaping the present clinical picture are inferable with reasonable confidence:

**Migration-cohort effect.** First-generation immigration from a South Asian, Muslim-majority sending society to a post-9/11 U.S. metropolitan periphery (Jersey City) reliably produces a parenting style organized around vigilance, cultural transmission anxiety, and respectability politics. Muneeba's profile is *modal* for this cohort, not extreme within it. The acculturation-gap-distress literature (Telzer; Birman) describes exactly the mother-daughter dynamic the Wilson run dramatizes.

**Religious-practice integration.** Muneeba's Islam is observed, not theorized. Five-times-daily salah, Ramadan, halal household, hijab in public — these constitute a high-frequency, body-anchored ritual architecture that functions, in psychiatric terms, as an extremely effective distress-tolerance and meaning-making system. Subjects with comparable practice intensity show lower rates of complicated bereavement and depression in the actual outcome literature (Pargament; Abu-Raiya). This is a protective factor of the first order in her file.

**Stable pair-bond.** Yusuf is depicted across writers as affectionate, present, and aligned with Muneeba on values. The marriage is the single largest protective variable after religious practice. Loss of Yusuf, when it eventually occurs (his cardiac history makes the actuarial picture clear), is the most probable precipitant for any future decompensation.

**Probable premigration baseline.** Inferable rather than depicted: Muneeba presents as someone who *arrived* with intact attachment security, intact executive function, and intact role-identity. There is no behavioral trace of childhood trauma, parentification scarring, or family-of-origin instability. Her capacity to revise her model of her own children on evidence — non-trivial under stress — argues for a premorbid baseline of cognitive flexibility laid down well before migration.

**Stressor history, cumulative.** Two near-end-of-world events, one spouse cardiac event, one occupation of her city by hostile actors, one child's death, one child's resurrection-as-mutant. Civilian baseline. The fact that this load has not produced symptomatic decompensation is, again, the central finding.

---

## 4.4 The Differential — What She Is NOT, and Why

Each candidate diagnosis below is one a clinician seeing Muneeba on a single occasion, or working from a non-longitudinal slice, could plausibly raise. Each is then ruled out on specific evidentiary grounds.

### 4.4.1 Generalized Anxiety Disorder (300.02 / F41.1)

**Why considered:** chronic worry about a child's safety; somatic readiness (the scanning, the tightness around the shoulders depicted in Alphona's line); difficulty "letting go" of concern.

**Why rejected:**
- *Content specificity.* GAD requires worry across multiple domains, free-floating, often shifting target. Muneeba's worry is anchored to specific real referents (Kamala, Yusuf, family standing) and does not migrate.
- *No somatic criterion satisfaction.* No depicted insomnia, no muscle tension complaints, no fatigue, no irritability cluster, no concentration impairment.
- *Functional impairment absent.* She executes role demands at a high level. GAD requires clinically significant impairment.
- *Proportionality.* Her worry tracks actual risk in her environment with calibration that is, if anything, *under*-tuned — she correctly identified Kamala's heroism and did not panic.

### 4.4.2 Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder (301.4 / F60.5)

**Why considered:** rule-orientation; orderliness; moral certainty on principles; tight household standards.

**Why rejected:**
- *Updates on evidence.* The cardinal feature of OCPD is rigidity against disconfirming information. Muneeba updates — on Aamir's religiosity, on Tyesha's sincerity, on Kamala's heroism, on Bruno across the years.
- *Capacity for warmth.* OCPD characteristically interferes with affectionate expression. Muneeba is physically and verbally tender with Yusuf and, under duress, with Kamala. The capacity is present and undefended.
- *No hoarding, no perfectionism beyond task-completion threshold, no over-conscientiousness about money or work.* The criterion set is not met.
- *Ego-syntony is in the wrong place.* OCPD subjects experience their rigidity as virtue; Muneeba experiences her *role* as virtue and her rules as instruments. This is the diagnostic hinge: instrumental rule-use is parenting style, terminal rule-use is OCPD.

### 4.4.3 Major Depressive Disorder, recurrent or single episode (296.x / F32–33)

**Why considered:** bereavement of her child; muted affect in public; cultural-religious idiom that could mask depressive cognition.

**Why rejected:**
- *No anhedonia.* Post-bereavement, she continues to take observable pleasure in cooking, in Yusuf, in community ritual, in Aamir's family.
- *No vegetative cluster depicted.* No sleep disturbance, no appetite change, no psychomotor change.
- *No worthlessness or excessive guilt.* Her grief is sad and reverent, not self-attacking. She does not blame herself for Kamala's death in the depressive-cognition register, though she does mourn it.
- *No suicidal ideation, passive or active.*
- *Preserved future-orientation.* She continues to plan, to invest in Aamir's child, to maintain the household — depressed subjects characteristically lose this.

A *situational depressive reaction* in the bereavement window is plausible at subclinical magnitude but does not reach episode threshold.

### 4.4.4 Persistent Complex Bereavement Disorder / Prolonged Grief Disorder (F43.81 in ICD-11)

**Why considered:** loss of a child is the highest-risk bereavement; her cultural-religious idiom could be misread as either resolution or pathological avoidance.

**Why rejected:**
- *Time-course.* PGD requires symptoms persisting beyond 6–12 months post-loss with significant impairment. Muneeba's grief is intense but integrative — she incorporates Kamala's memory into the household's ongoing life rather than freezing around it.
- *No identity disruption.* She remains Muneeba — wife, mother, community member — through the loss. PGD typically involves disorganization of self-concept around the loss.
- *No avoidance of reminders.* She speaks of Kamala, keeps her artifacts, accepts visitors who knew her.
- *No bitterness or intense emotional pain meeting criterion.* The pain is present and depicted; the qualitative register is grief, not the specific PGD phenomenology of unrelenting yearning with functional collapse.
- *The resurrection complicates but does not reverse this assessment.* A grief that successfully integrates and is then complicated by the deceased's actual return is a case the diagnostic manuals do not contemplate; clinically, her response (acceptance with worry, the established pattern) is the most adaptive available.

### 4.4.5 Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (309.81 / F43.10)

**Why considered:** repeated exposure to extinction-level threat events; spouse's near-death cardiac event; child's death.

**Why rejected:**
- *No intrusive re-experiencing depicted.* No flashbacks, no nightmares of record, no intrusive imagery commentary.
- *No avoidance cluster.* She does not avoid hospitals (managed Yusuf's cardiac care), does not avoid sites of trauma, does not avoid trauma-linked persons.
- *No negative alterations in cognition and mood beyond the bereavement-appropriate.*
- *No hyperarousal beyond her baseline targeted vigilance,* which predates the trauma exposures.
- The Incursion events specifically appear to have been *integrated through religious meaning-making* (the *Last Days* praying-together scene) rather than encoded as trauma. This is the protective mechanism doing its work in real time on the page.

### 4.4.6 Adjustment Disorder (309.x / F43.2)

**Why considered:** any of the major stressor events could plausibly precipitate one.

**Why rejected:** the diagnosis requires symptoms in excess of what would be expected and/or significant impairment. Muneeba's reactions are consistently *commensurate* with the precipitants and do not impair role function. The diagnosis would be a category error applied to her.

### 4.4.7 Avoidant or Dependent Personality Disorder

**Why considered (briefly):** her formality in public, her preference for known social circles.

**Why rejected:** she initiates and sustains relationships, leads in her household, navigates conflict directly when required, and shows no fear of negative evaluation in the AVPD sense — she navigates the gossip economy strategically, not avoidantly. Dependency fails on her demonstrated agency.

### 4.4.8 Schizoid / Schizotypal Spectrum

**Why considered:** the constricted public affect.

**Why rejected:** she has rich, reciprocal close relationships (Yusuf, the children, Auntie Ruby tier of confidantes), no odd beliefs outside her tradition's normal range, no perceptual disturbances, no social anhedonia. The constriction is cultural-stylistic, not schizoid.

### 4.4.9 Cultural / Religious Idiom Mistaken for Pathology

This is the differential clinicians most commonly fumble on subjects like Muneeba, and it warrants its own line. Behaviors that an under-attuned clinician could miscode:

- *Tawakkul* (reliance on God) miscoded as passive coping or learned helplessness — it is neither; it is an active meaning-making frame.
- *Modesty practice (hijab, gender-segregated socializing)* miscoded as social anxiety or AVPD-spectrum behavior — it is observed religious norm.
- *Reference to jinn, evil eye, or divine providence in causal attributions* — these are within-tradition explanatory frameworks, not delusional ideation. Muneeba uses such idiom sparingly but does use it; it is not psychotic content.
- *Suppression-dominant affect display* — within South Asian and broader Muslim cultural norms, this is the expected register for a woman of her age and standing, not anhedonia.

A culturally competent assessment must subtract these before any pathology coding. After subtraction, her presentation remains within normal limits.

### 4.4.10 Substance-Use Disorders

Categorically absent. Observant Muslim, no depicted alcohol or drug use, no behavioral-addiction features (no gambling, no compulsive shopping, no problematic technology use). Caffeine via chai is the only psychoactive intake of record.

---

## 4.5 Comorbidity Considerations

Because no primary diagnosis is supported, comorbidity is moot. The relevant note is that the *protective factors* in her file (religious practice, marriage, role-identity coherence, community embedding) are mutually reinforcing rather than competing, which is the architecture associated with the lowest lifetime psychiatric incidence in epidemiological samples of comparable demographics.

---

## 4.6 Course Over Time and Projected Trajectory

**2014–2016 (early Wilson):** baseline. Targeted hypervigilance at its highest pitch; this is the period of maximum acculturation-gap distress, with Kamala in mid-adolescence and the secret-identity load on the household at peak opacity.

**2016–2017 (mid-Wilson):** measurable de-escalation across the Ms. Marvel reveal. The reveal does not produce a crisis; it produces a *relaxation* in Muneeba, which is diagnostically meaningful — it confirms that the prior vigilance was load-bearing on incomplete information, not characterological.

**2017–2021 (Ahmed and after):** stable functioning. Yusuf's cardiac event introduces a new managed stressor; she absorbs it without symptomatic cost.

**2022–2023 (bereavement arc):** acute grief, contained presentation, no diagnostic threshold crossed. This is the highest-risk window in her file for a late-onset depressive episode, and the record's silence on such an episode is the strongest single piece of evidence for her resilience profile.

**2023–present (resurrection / mutant reveal):** the pattern holds. Acceptance with worry. No depicted destabilization from the metaphysical strangeness of the situation, which is itself notable — most subjects asked to integrate a resurrection event show at least transient derealization features.

**Projected risk windows:**

1. *Loss of Yusuf.* The highest-probability decompensation precipitant. With the pair-bond removed, religious practice and role-identity would have to carry load currently shared. A late-onset major depressive episode is plausible in this scenario; complicated grief less so, given her demonstrated grief-integration capacity.
2. *Migration of children out of immediate orbit / empty-nest dynamic in a culture where the multigenerational household is normative.* Moderate risk.
3. *A second loss of Kamala, were it to occur.* Unpredictable, but given the demonstrated capacity to absorb the first, the prior is toward integration rather than collapse.
4. *Community-level rejection event* (rare but possible, e.g., a public scandal involving the family) — her sensitivity to community standing makes this a non-trivial vector.

**Protective vectors expected to hold:** religious practice (extremely stable across the life course in this demographic), role identity (stable until widowhood), cognitive flexibility (a trait feature).

---

## 4.7 Treatment Recommendations (Hypothetical)

None indicated at present. Were she ever to present — most likely in the projected widowhood scenario — the indicated approach would be culturally adapted supportive therapy, ideally with a Muslim or Muslim-competent clinician, with explicit incorporation of her religious framework rather than against it; pharmacology only if a frank depressive episode emerged with vegetative features; *not* insight-oriented work attempting to dismantle her suppression-dominant style, which is the load-bearing wall of her functioning and not a symptom to be treated.

A culturally naive clinician attempting to "open her up" would do measurable harm. This is flagged for any future custodian of this file.

---

## 4.8 Summary Determination

Muneeba Khan presents, across approximately a decade of dense longitudinal observation and through stressor exposure that would diagnostically mark most civilian subjects, as **psychiatrically unremarkable**. The clinical interest of her file lies not in pathology but in the *architecture of her non-pathology* — the specific configuration of religious practice, role-identity coherence, suppression-dominant defense, secure attachment, and culturally-modal parenting that has, in the published record, held against everything her life has put through it.

The container has held. The dossier's job is to note exactly how, and to flag the conditions under which it would not.

*End Section 04. Proceed to Section 05 — Personality Structure & Operating Code.*


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: MUNEEBA KHAN

*Classification: Stage-Two Granular Mapping. Cross-referenced to Stage-One workup. Read longitudinally; the same body produces different signatures under different loads, and the diagnostic value is in the delta.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM STATE

The calm Muneeba is the hardest to read because she has spent decades making her calm legible only as *order*. The baseline signatures are environmental before they are somatic — you locate her by the state of the rooms she has passed through.

**Domestic kinetics.** She moves through the Jersey City house on a fixed circuit: kitchen → dining table → hallway lamp → Yusuf's reading chair → kitchen. The circuit is closed; she rarely sits for longer than ten minutes outside the kitchen island unless prayer, guests, or television with Yusuf draws her into the living room. When seated, she sits *forward* — never reclined — with both feet flat on the floor, dupatta over one shoulder if uncovered, hijab pin checked at the temple if covered.

**Hand language.** Her hands are almost never still and almost never in her lap. They are wiping a counter, folding a dishtowel into thirds (always thirds, never halves), adjusting a salt shaker by half an inch, straightening a stack of mail by tapping the long edge twice on the table. The tapping is the calm tell: two short taps to align an edge means she is content. Three taps, slower, means she is thinking about something she has not raised yet.

**Vocal register at rest.** A measured alto in Urdu, a slightly higher and more clipped register in English. She code-switches mid-sentence by reflex; the English clauses tend to carry instructions and the Urdu clauses tend to carry feeling. Volume baseline is low — she does not raise her voice to summon anyone in the house; she expects you to be within earshot, and she expects you to come.

**Eye behavior.** Sustained gaze on the person she is addressing only in the home. In public her eyes track middle distance and ground; she rarely meets the eyes of unrelated men, a practiced modesty rather than shyness. With Kamala she has a specific look — a half-second hold, eyebrows neutral, that functions as a question mark; with Aamir she rarely uses it because she does not need to.

**Food as ambient communication.** Calm Muneeba cooks in a measured 90-minute block in the late afternoon. Pots simmer; she does not stand over them; she sets timers in her head and is never wrong by more than a minute. The smell signature of a calm house: cumin bloomed in oil, onions browning slowly, rice resting under a folded towel. When the kitchen smells of *more* than this — when she is cooking three things that do not belong to one meal — she is displacing something.

**Devotional rhythm.** Five prayers, on time, with mild flexibility for Maghrib if guests are present. Wudu performed at the bathroom sink with the door ajar — not from immodesty but from a lifelong habit of keeping ears on the house. Janamaz unrolled in the same square of the bedroom, oriented by a piece of tape on the baseboard Yusuf placed there in 2009 and she has never asked him to remove. Post-prayer dhikr counted on the fingers of the right hand, not on tasbih beads — beads are for grief or supplication, fingers are for routine.

**Sleep and waking.** Wakes for Fajr without alarm; has done so for thirty years. Tea before prayer in a specific small cup (chipped on the inner rim, never replaced). Reads the Urdu newspaper at the kitchen table for twenty minutes before the household stirs. This is the only window in the twenty-four-hour cycle when she is reliably alone and reliably still, and it is the window in which she does her most honest thinking. Anyone who needed to read her unguarded would observe her between 5:15 and 5:45 a.m.

---

## II. UNDER LOW-GRADE STRESS (the modal condition)

Low-grade stress is Muneeba's most-occupied state across the published record — the chronic background hum of immigrant-parent vigilance. The signatures are subtle and *additive*; she does not look stressed, she looks *more like herself*.

**The tightening pattern.** Rules multiply. Curfew advances by thirty minutes. A previously approved friend is suddenly "that girl whose mother I don't know well." Phone is to be left on the kitchen counter at night. None of this is announced as a response to a stressor; it arrives as if it had always been policy. The diagnostic is the *rate of accretion*: when three new rules appear in a week, something has alarmed her that she has not yet named.

**Surface composure tells.** She begins to iron things that do not need ironing. Dupattas, pillowcases, Yusuf's already-pressed shirts. The iron is a regulatory object for her; the hiss of steam and the repetitive sweep displace what she will not verbalize. Adjacent: she rearranges the spice drawer. If the spice drawer has been reorganized, the household has been under load for at least seventy-two hours.

**Micro-verbal tells.** Sentences shorten. The interrogatives become declaratives — "where were you" loses the question mark and becomes a statement she expects you to fill in. She says *beta* more frequently and more flatly; the endearment is doing the work of softening a directive she does not want to soften.

**Phone behavior.** Calls to her sister in Karachi increase in frequency but shorten in duration. The calls are made from the back porch, not the kitchen, which means she does not want them overheard. She does not gossip on these calls; she *checks in*, which is her way of confirming that the wider family architecture is intact while one local element is wobbling.

**Decision habit under low stress:** *delay and observe.* She does not act on suspicion. She gathers. She watches Kamala's face at dinner over the rim of her chai. She notes who calls the landline and who does not. She will sit on a concern for days before raising it, and when she raises it she will already have the disposition decided.

---

## III. UNDER ACUTE STRESS (sharp, contained crisis)

Acute stress in Muneeba's record is associated with discoveries — a lie uncovered, a friend's bad influence confirmed, an unexpected school call, the first time Yusuf complained of chest tightness. The signature shifts from accretive to compressed.

**Physical compression.** Shoulders rise approximately a centimeter and stay there. Jaw set, lips drawn slightly inward. Breath shortens but does not become audible — she is a quiet stress-breather; you can only see it in the rise of the collarbone. The dupatta is gathered tighter to the throat with the left hand, an unconscious gesture of self-containment that she has been observed making since at least the first year of the published record.

**Cold withdrawal.** Her single most-reliable disciplinary tool. She does not raise her voice; she lowers her *availability*. Food is still cooked, plates are still set, but the conversational warmth she usually provides is withdrawn. Direct address is replaced by third-person — "your sister will not eat with us tonight," spoken to Aamir while Kamala is in the room. The treatment is intentionally legible and intentionally finite; it ends when the offending party initiates repair.

**The pause.** When confronted with information she did not expect, she pauses for a beat that is too long for ordinary conversation — perhaps two full seconds — before responding. The pause is not searching; it is *sorting*. She is deciding which version of her response to deliver. Anyone watching can see the version change.

**Decision habit under acute stress:** *seal the perimeter, then assess.* She first contains the household — no one leaves, no calls are made, no public mention — and only then evaluates what has actually happened. The instinct is reputational and structural before it is investigative.

**What does not happen.** No shouting. No tears in front of others. No striking. No threat. The ceiling she will not cross is enforcement-through-fear. Whatever Muneeba's grandparents may have used, she has chosen — and the consistency across the published record is the evidence of choice, not absence — not to.

---

## IV. UNDER GENUINE THREAT (catastrophic, existential)

The signature here is the inverse of the acute-stress signature. This is the most important non-obvious feature of her behavioral profile.

**The role-drop.** When a situation crosses from manageable into truly catastrophic — the Incursion in *Last Days*, Yusuf collapsing, the confirmed news of Kamala's death — Muneeba sets down the entire enforcement apparatus *immediately and without transition*. The rules disappear. The cold withdrawal disappears. The composed alto disappears. What is left is unmediated maternal presence: hands on her child's face, forehead against forehead, prayer spoken aloud rather than internally.

**Physical contact threshold collapses.** A woman who in calm baseline rarely initiates hug-length contact with her adult children will, under existential threat, hold Kamala for minutes at a time without speaking, palms flat on her daughter's back, rocking imperceptibly. The contact is the communication; she does not narrate it.

**Voice change.** The clipped English vanishes entirely. She speaks only Urdu under genuine threat, and within the Urdu register she shifts toward the older, softer vocabulary of her own mother — diminutives, lullaby cadences, *meri jaan, meri bachi*. This is the voice she has otherwise kept private for thirty years.

**Decisional simplification.** All deliberation collapses to one criterion: where is the child, and how do I be with them. Logistics that would normally occupy her — what the neighbors think, what is appropriate, what is on the stove — fall away completely. This is not panic; it is *priority resolution*. The hierarchy was always there; threat just exposes it.

**Prayer under threat.** Audible, hands open in front of her rather than folded, often with Kamala's hand pulled into her own. She does not perform composure at this register; she performs *connection*, to God and to the child, in the same breath.

---

## V. INTIMACY (with Yusuf, with each child, with the inner circle)

Intimacy is a rationed and channel-specific behavior in Muneeba's repertoire. Different relationships receive different signatures; she does not have one mode of closeness.

**With Yusuf.** The marriage is depicted as steady and tender, and the intimacy tells are mostly small and domestic. She refills his tea without asking. She knows the precise sequence of his cardiac medications and lays them out next to his breakfast in a small saucer. She touches his shoulder in passing — a quick squeeze, not a stroke — at least three or four times a day. They share a private register of jokes about their courtship and early marriage that the children catch only the edges of. In disagreement, she defers in public and argues in private; in private, the arguments are conducted in low voices with the bedroom door closed, and end with her bringing him chai an hour later, which is her apology even when she was not in the wrong.

**With Aamir.** The intimacy is mock-exasperated. She tolerates his religiosity with a register of tongue-clucks and head-shakes that he and she both understand to be affection. She feeds him preferentially; the largest portion always lands on his plate. She does not interrogate him about his choices because she trusts the moral substrate. With his wife Tyesha, after an initial cool period she settles into a daughter-in-law register that is warm but deliberately *educational* — passing recipes, demonstrating folds of a dupatta, teaching her Urdu kitchen vocabulary, all of which are how she absorbs people into the family architecture rather than how she tests them.

**With Kamala.** The most complicated channel and the one that consumes the most of her attention. Pre-revelation, intimacy is delivered obliquely — through food prepared specifically to Kamala's preference without acknowledgment, through brushing hair out of her daughter's eyes mid-lecture, through quiet entry into Kamala's room at night to pull up a blanket Kamala has kicked off. Post-revelation, intimacy is more direct: she initiates conversations about Kamala's day-as-Ms.-Marvel with deliberate casualness, the way one would ask about a child's job. She has learned, slowly, to ask before correcting.

**With the masjid circle and Auntie Ruby.** Sociable but never confiding. She offers second helpings, laughs at the right moments, asks after grandchildren by name, and reveals nothing of her own household's interior. She is liked and trusted but not, in the deep sense, *known* by anyone outside Yusuf and her sister in Karachi.

---

## VI. GRIEF

The grief signature is the densest section of this file because it is the longest-documented sustained affect state in the published record.

**Public composure.** At the janazah and in the days that follow, she holds the line. Receives condolences with both hands extended, says *JazakAllah khair* in a controlled voice, accepts food without protest, seats guests without fuss. The composure is not denial; it is a form of *service*. She has decided that the community needs her grief to be conductable, and she conducts.

**Private collapse.** Behind doors, the body that held itself a centimeter tighter under acute stress now slackens entirely. She sits, which she almost never does in baseline. She sits in Kamala's room on the edge of the bed, often for an hour at a time, hands open in her lap, not crying continuously but in irregular waves. The tasbih beads reappear — the ones she does not use for ordinary dhikr — and move through her fingers steadily, ninety-nine, ninety-nine, ninety-nine.

**Sensory anchoring.** She handles Kamala's things in a specific order: the dupatta first, then a school notebook, then a hairbrush. She does not wash the hairbrush. She does not move anything in the room. When she finally permits herself to wash a single item of Kamala's clothing weeks later, it is depicted as a deliberate, ritualized act, performed by hand at the kitchen sink rather than in the machine.

**Sleep disturbance.** Wakes earlier than Fajr — 4:30, 4:00, eventually 3:45. The pre-dawn window expands and the reading at the kitchen table is replaced by long quiet sitting. Tea is still made; it goes cold. Yusuf, who knows her completely, lets her have the silence.

**Functional preservation.** She continues to cook, to receive guests, to manage Yusuf's medications, to attend the masjid. The infrastructure she built to contain catastrophe holds. This is not avoidance; the grief is metabolizing inside the structure, not being deflected by it. The distinction is visible in her face, which thins, ages, and develops a new stillness around the eyes that persists into subsequent appearances.

**Religious framework as integrative.** She speaks of Kamala in the past tense without flinching and in the prayer-frame without bitterness. *Inna lillahi wa inna ilayhi raji'un* is said aloud, in full, multiple times a day. The framework is doing genuine work; it is not platitude. It is the cognitive container §3 identified, performing exactly the function it was built for.

---

## VII. VICTORY / RELIEF

Victory in Muneeba's vocabulary is not triumph. It is *exhalation*. The tells are quiet.

**Somatic relief.** The shoulders drop. The dupatta is loosened at the throat. The half-second pause before speech disappears. She makes tea — not because anyone asked, but because tea is her gesture of *the danger has passed*.

**Verbal tell.** A short Urdu phrase of thanks to God, half-whispered, often delivered with eyes closed for a single breath. Not performative; reflexive. Anyone who has spent ten minutes with her has heard it; few register it as significant.

**Indirect celebration.** She does not praise her children to their faces in moments of success. She praises them to others *in their hearing*. A phone call to her sister, conducted in the kitchen rather than on the porch, in which she recounts the success in detail — that is the celebration, and the children are meant to overhear it. The architecture is intentional. She protects them from the evil eye on the surface and protects them from her own embarrassment about overt pride underneath.

**Decision habit after victory:** *immediate return to baseline.* She does not linger in relief. She resumes the chores she set down. The dishtowel is folded into thirds again within minutes. Victory is not a state she inhabits; it is a checkpoint she passes.

---

## VIII. DEFEAT / SHAME

Defeat for Muneeba is rarely operational and almost always relational — a moment in which she has been shown to have misread a situation or mis-handled a person she loves.

**The honesty reflex.** When she has been wrong, she acknowledges it, but with characteristic indirection. She does not say "I am sorry"; she says, "I should have listened," or she demonstrates the apology behaviorally — cooking the person's preferred dish, sitting beside them on the couch instead of across from them, asking about something she previously dismissed.

**With Kamala specifically.** The post-revelation arc is one long, distributed apology for the surveillance years, and the form it takes is *deferral*. She lets Kamala finish sentences she would once have interrupted. She asks before correcting. She accepts decisions she would not have accepted before. The shift is gradual and dignified; she does not perform contrition, she enacts revision.

**Public shame.** Her sharpest pressure point. A community-visible failure — a child's misbehavior reported back through the masjid circle, an implication that the household is not what it presents — produces the only behavior in her repertoire that approaches genuine harshness: a tight-lipped silence that lasts through an entire meal, and a subsequent week of intensified rule-enforcement directed at whoever caused the exposure. Even here, no shouting; the cost is paid in withdrawn warmth, which she knows to be the more expensive currency.

**Self-directed shame.** Hardest to observe. The tell is liturgical: increased frequency of nafl prayer, longer sujood, the tasbih beads back in her hand outside grief context. When she is privately ashamed of herself, she takes it to God rather than to Yusuf.

---

## IX. DECEPTION DETECTION AND TRUTH-TELLING

**Reading lies.** She is exceptionally good at it and the children know it. The reading apparatus is *baseline-comparative*: she has decades of data on each child's micro-behaviors and notices deviation immediately. Kamala averting her eyes for half a second longer than usual at dinner, Aamir's voice carrying a faint defensive register, Yusuf taking the second piece of bread before he has finished the first — all read. She does not always confront. She *files*. The confrontation, if it comes, may be days later.

**Telling lies.** She does not lie to her family in any cited material; she withholds. The distinction is operational. The Ms. Marvel knowledge held for months is the canonical example: she had the information, did not deploy it, and did not pretend to lack it — she simply did not raise it. This is her characteristic posture toward dangerous truths: hold them silently until the moment of disclosure is also the moment of integration.

**To outsiders.** She is socially polished and selectively candid. The masjid circle gets the curated household; the school administrators get the composed mother; the doctors get a precise medical history of Yusuf with nothing extraneous. None of this is dishonesty; it is *boundary-keeping*. She regards her family's interior as not owed to outsiders.

---

## X. CONFLICT, CONFRONTATION, AND THE ESCALATION LADDER

The ladder, in operational order:

1. **Observation, unannounced.** She watches and files. No external signature beyond marginal increase in attentiveness.
2. **Subtle rule-tightening.** Curfew, phone, friends. Delivered without explanation.
3. **Cold withdrawal.** Warmth retracted; food still cooked; conversation reduced to logistics. This is the disciplinary mode she relies on most.
4. **Direct verbal confrontation, private.** Conducted in Urdu, low volume, in the kitchen or the bedroom, never in front of guests. The structure is always: *here is what I observed, here is what it means, here is what will change.* She does not litigate; she rules.
5. **Confrontation with Yusuf as co-signatory.** Reserved for matters she considers grave. Yusuf is brought in not to overrule her but to underline her. Once it reaches this rung, the matter is settled.
6. **Withdrawal of a privilege at family-system level.** Rare. Used only on conduct she regards as morally — not behaviorally — wrong.
7. **In existential crisis, ladder collapses entirely.** See §IV.

She does not have a rung labeled rage. She does not have a rung labeled physical discipline. She does not have a rung labeled estrangement. The ceiling is cold withdrawal followed by an offered return; the floor is unconditional presence. Between these she has built a remarkably narrow but remarkably durable corridor in which she has, across the published record, conducted the entire emotional life of her household.

---

## XI. RITUAL, ROUTE, AND CALENDAR

**Daily.** Fajr at home; brief morning reading; breakfast laid out for Yusuf and whoever else is awake; midmorning errands (grocery, pharmacy for Yusuf's prescriptions, occasional masjid drop-off); Zuhr; afternoon cooking block; Asr; family dinner, ideally with all present; Maghrib; television hour with Yusuf; Isha; sleep by 10:30.

**Weekly.** Friday is the structural anchor — house is cleaner, food is more elaborate, Yusuf attends Jumu'ah. Saturday is for community visits or hosting. Sunday is for rest and for letters/calls to Karachi.

**Annual.** Ramadan reorganizes the entire household around her — suhoor and iftar prep, increased Qur'an recitation, charitable giving she manages personally rather than delegating. Eid is the year's other anchor; she cooks for two days in advance and hosts. Birthdays are observed minimally and Islamically — a prayer, a sweet, no candles. The death anniversary, after the loss, becomes a quiet private observance she conducts mostly alone, in Kamala's room, in the early morning.

**Routes.** She drives the same three or four routes — to the masjid, to the South Asian grocer, to the pharmacy, to Aamir and Tyesha's place. She does not explore. She knows which cashier at the grocer asks about her family and which does not, and she calibrates her warmth accordingly. She parks in the same spot at the masjid lot, second row from the entrance, left side, because it is closest to the women's door.

---

## XII. THE DIAGNOSTIC SUMMARY OF TELLS

If one had to read Muneeba Khan in real time without prior context, the highest-yield observations, in order:

1. The dishtowel: how many folds, how recently re-folded.
2. The dupatta at the throat: loose, gathered, or gripped.
3. The shoulder line, relative to her own neutral.
4. The length of pause before her reply.
5. The ratio of Urdu to English in the sentence.
6. Whether she is sitting at all, and if so, where.
7. Whether the tasbih beads are in her hand.
8. Whether the kitchen smells of one meal or three.
9. Whether her eyes have held the addressee for the half-second question.
10. Whether tea has been offered without request.

These ten readings, taken together, will place her on the spectrum from calm baseline through grief with greater reliability than any verbal self-report she would ever consent to give. She has spent a lifetime keeping the interior private; she has not, because she could not, kept the surface from telling the truth.

*End Behavio


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DOSSIER SECTION — DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

## SUBJECT: MUNEEBA KHAN

*A composite week of total-surveillance observation, cross-referenced against canonical depiction (Wilson 2014–2019; Ahmed 2019–2021; bereavement and post-resurrection material 2022–present). Inferences extrapolate from the household's documented rhythms.*

---

## 1. THE ARCHITECTURE OF HER DAY

Muneeba Khan's life is structured by two overlapping clocks: the **liturgical clock** (the five daily prayers, which move across the year with the sun) and the **household clock** (school runs, meal preparation, Yusuf's medication schedule, the rhythm of her cleaning rotation). These two clocks do not always agree, and the small adjustments she makes to reconcile them — moving Asr earlier so she can put rice on, holding Maghrib until Yusuf is home from the masjid so they can pray together — are the most reliable behavioral fingerprint in the file. A surveillance log of her week would show extraordinary regularity: the same rooms at the same hours, the same external errands on the same weekdays, deviations of no more than fifteen minutes from a baseline pattern unless something is wrong.

The Jersey City house — modest, two-story, attached, in a South Asian and Arab neighborhood of Greenville — is her primary theater of operations. She leaves it, on a typical week, perhaps six to nine times: groceries (Tuesday and Friday), the halal butcher (Friday), the masjid (Friday afternoon with Yusuf, sometimes Sunday for women's halaqa), a school or community event, and one or two social visits. She does not commute. The published material is unspecific on whether she holds outside paid employment in the present era; the household reads as one in which her labor is the domestic infrastructure that allows Yusuf's professional life and the children's education to function, and the dossier treats her accordingly. Her workplace is the house.

---

## 2. PRE-DAWN AND MORNING (FAJR THROUGH BREAKFAST)

She is, by the testimony of the household's depicted rhythms, an early riser by necessity rather than disposition. **Fajr** — the dawn prayer — sets the floor. In summer this can mean a 4:15 a.m. alarm; in winter, closer to 6:00. She wakes, performs **wudu** in the small downstairs bathroom (the upstairs one is the children's territory and louder plumbing would wake them), prays on the living-room musallah she keeps rolled behind the sofa, and reads a short portion of Qur'an afterward — usually from a worn paperback mushaf with a green cover, a tasbih on the side table. In summer when Fajr is very early, she frequently goes back to bed for an hour; in winter she stays up.

Between Fajr and the rest of the house waking, she has roughly forty-five minutes that are functionally hers. Surveillance would record: the kettle on (chai, not coffee — black tea, cardamom pod cracked between her fingers, full-fat milk, sugar measured by eye but consistent to within half a teaspoon), the kitchen radio low on a news station, the previous night's dishes finished, the day's chicken or meat moved from freezer to thaw. She uses this window for the work she does not want to be interrupted: paying bills, opening official mail, sometimes a phone call to Karachi (the time difference makes early-morning Jersey late-afternoon there).

By 6:45 she is moving through the upstairs, knocking on doors. The household is not military — the children, in their respective eras, are habitual oversleepers — but Muneeba's tolerance for repeated waking calls is finite and audibly degrades. The third knock is harder than the first. **Breakfast** is laid out rather than served: toast, fruit, eggs if anyone has the time, the previous night's parathas reheated if there were any. Kamala, canonically, eats fast and badly in the morning; Muneeba comments on this most days and is largely ignored. She herself eats little — half a paratha, more tea — and stands while doing it, watching the kitchen clock.

Yusuf leaves first. She walks him to the door more often than not, hands him a packed lunch when his cardiac diet requires it (post-Ahmed run, this is daily — measured portions, low sodium, the salt shaker quietly relocated to a high shelf in her own kitchen), and reminds him of his medications by name and time. The reminder is delivered as if it were a casual remark; it is not casual.

---

## 3. MID-MORNING (THE WORKING HOURS OF THE HOUSE)

With the house empty between roughly 8:30 and 3:00, she enters what is observably her most autonomous block of the day. This is when the **deep housework** happens — not the daily wipe-down but the rotating projects: Monday laundry (sorted by owner and color, hung when weather permits because she dislikes the dryer's effect on her good clothes), Tuesday the kitchen deep-clean (stovetop, fridge interior on a fortnightly cycle), Wednesday bathrooms, Thursday floors, Friday the cooking marathon for **Jummah** and the weekend, Saturday lighter, Sunday the formal living-room dusting that nobody else is allowed to disturb.

A surveillance file would note that she **does not multitask the way younger women in her circle do**. She finishes one task before opening another. She does not have music or television on during cleaning; she will sometimes have a recitation of Qur'an playing low from her phone, particularly during repetitive work. She talks to herself in Urdu under her breath while working — short phrases, complaints, ruminations, dua. This is one of the most reliable behavioral tells in the file: when she is upset, the muttering increases; when she is content, she hums (no identifiable melody, often the cadence of a nasheed).

**Mid-morning phone calls** are her primary social channel. Auntie Ruby is the most frequent correspondent — calls that can run forty minutes, conducted while Muneeba is doing something else with her hands (chopping, folding). She holds the phone between shoulder and ear in the old way; she has not adopted a headset. The content of these calls is canonically gossip-adjacent — community marriages, illnesses, scandals — but the surveillance read is more accurate as **intelligence-gathering**: she is mapping the community's social terrain so that she knows in advance which families are credible, which are not, who is marriageable, who is in trouble. Kamala underestimates the strategic content of these calls throughout the early run.

**Dhuhr** falls in the middle of this block. She prays alone, on the same musallah, in roughly six to eight minutes including the sunnah. She does not rush the prayer but she does not extend it; her relationship to the obligatory acts is one of consistent observance rather than performative piety.

**Cooking** is the day's primary creative act. She begins the evening meal between 1:30 and 3:00 depending on what it is — biryani is a half-day commitment begun in late morning; daal and a sabzi can be assembled in forty minutes. She does not measure spices. She does not consult recipes. The kitchen is organized by her logic and resists reorganization: spices in repurposed pickle jars on a specific shelf, atta in a tin under the counter, the good knife in a drawer she opens without looking. Anyone who moves something is corrected immediately and remembers not to do it again.

---

## 4. AFTERNOON (THE RETURN OF THE CHILDREN)

The house's center of gravity shifts at roughly 3:00 when school lets out. In the Kamala-in-residence era this is when Muneeba's **monitoring function** activates most visibly. A week of surveillance would document a near-invariant sequence: the door, the call of *Assalamu alaikum* (Kamala's response delivered in motion, already moving toward the stairs), Muneeba's intercept question — *where were you, who was with you, did you eat, did you pray Dhuhr* — delivered as a sequence with no pause for answers, then the actual extraction of information, which happens at the kitchen table over a snack Muneeba has prepared and presents as casually as if she had not been timing the door.

This ritual is the single most-documented behavioral pattern in her file. It is the place where her **control-as-proxy-for-connection** mechanism is most visible: she wants to know how her daughter is, and she asks by enforcing rules. The snack — usually something hot, fried, or both, deployed at a calorie level that overrides Kamala's hurry — is the affection inside the surveillance.

**Asr** is prayed in this window, sometimes with whichever daughter is home, more often alone. After Asr, Muneeba's tempo slows perceptibly. This is her **rest hour**, the only one in her day. She sits on the living room couch — same end, the one nearer the window — and either watches a Pakistani drama serial (she has long-running attachment to certain shows and will adjust her schedule for the finale of a serial she has followed for months), reads, or naps for twenty to thirty minutes. The naps are short and she denies taking them.

---

## 5. EVENING (THE GATHERING)

**Maghrib** is the day's social prayer. When Yusuf is home, they pray together — he leads, she stands behind, a small choreography practiced over decades. If the children are present and willing they join; if not, Muneeba does not press in the moment but logs it for later mention. Dinner follows almost immediately. The table is set properly: actual plates, water in a jug, salad if there is one, achaar in a small dish. Eating in front of the television is permitted on weekends and discouraged on weekdays. Muneeba eats last and slowest — she serves, watches the consumption, refills, and only when everyone else is well into the meal does she sit and eat herself. This is not a martyrdom posture; it is the management posture of a woman who has been feeding a family for thirty years and prefers to oversee the operation.

**Conversation at dinner** in the early run is reliably tense between mother and daughter and warmer between mother and son. Yusuf moderates with mild humor. After the meal Muneeba clears (Kamala is required to help and frequently does so badly), and the family disperses — Yusuf to the news, the children to homework or rooms.

**Isha**, the night prayer, comes late, especially in summer. She prays it later than strictly required when she is finishing something, but she does not skip it. After Isha she reads — often a religious book, sometimes a novel in Urdu — for thirty to sixty minutes on the couch, in her dupatta but without the structured outer hijab she wears when male non-mahram guests are expected.

She is usually in bed by 11:00 in winter, later in summer when prayers themselves are later. She and Yusuf talk in bed before sleeping — the day's debrief, in Urdu, low voices, the door cracked so they can hear if anyone is up. This is the part of her life least visible to her children and arguably the most important load-bearing structure of her psychology: the marital conversation is where she off-loads the day's worry. When this conversation is unavailable (Yusuf away, Yusuf hospitalized) her sleep degrades measurably — she rises earlier, eats less, increases the muttering.

---

## 6. THE WEEKLY CYCLE

**Friday** is the week's vertical axis. The cooking is heavier (mutton or chicken karahi, fresh rotis, often a sweet — kheer, halwa, sometimes a store-bought mithai if she is short on time). She dresses with more care — a pressed shalwar kameez, the better dupatta, the silver bangles rather than the everyday ones, attar instead of nothing. She accompanies Yusuf to the masjid for Jummah when she can, prays in the women's section, and stays afterward for the brief social aperture in which the women's community business is conducted — who is sick, whose daughter is engaged, whose son is moving back from Houston. She extracts more information in this twenty minutes than from a week of phone calls.

**Saturday** is the elastic day — extended family visits, hosting or being hosted, shopping for things not available at the regular grocery (the Devon Avenue trip if she is in Chicago visiting relatives; the equivalent Jersey or Edison runs locally). She does not relax exactly; she shifts the work from maintenance to projection. Saturday is when she also engages in **community labor** — bringing food to a household with a new baby or a recent death, attending a milad, contributing to a fundraiser. This is canonical for her cohort and consistent with the perceptiveness §3 noted.

**Sunday** is the closest she comes to a sabbath. The house is cleaned only lightly. She often watches a longer afternoon program. The children are more likely to be home and she is more likely to attempt **the soft version** of the mother-daughter conversation, with mixed results. She may attend a women's halaqa at the masjid or hold one informally in her own living room on rotation.

---

## 7. HABITS OF THE BODY

Surveillance-grade granularity:

- **Posture:** upright, shoulders squared even when tired. She does not slump even when alone. When she finally does — kitchen chair, late at night, hand on her forehead — it is a reliable sign of unusual distress.
- **Hands:** in constant low-grade motion. When not occupied she rotates her wedding ring with her thumb, or runs her tasbih beads without counting. Anxiety raises the speed; grief slows it almost to stillness.
- **Gait:** brisk indoors, slower outdoors. She walks like a woman who knows the layout of her own house in the dark, which she does.
- **Voice:** low-pitched, controlled, with a register shift between Urdu (warmer, more melodic, more curse-adjacent expression) and English (clipped, deliberate, slightly formal). She code-switches mid-sentence with her children, full Urdu with peers, mostly English with Tyesha out of respect (though she has been observably teaching Tyesha kitchen vocabulary).
- **Eye contact:** direct with women, modulated with men by relation (full with Yusuf, mahram males; lower and briefer with non-mahram).
- **Touch:** sparing in public, freer in private. She touches her children's faces, hair, hands when she greets them after any absence, however short. The frequency of this physical greeting *increased* visibly post-revelation and again after the resurrection arc — a quiet, repeated re-verification.
- **Dress:** hijab and abaya or loose outer layer in public; shalwar kameez at home; the dupatta is on or near her at all times even indoors. She owns perhaps eight or nine everyday outfits in rotation and three or four "good" ones. Clothing is mended rather than replaced. She iron-presses her own dupattas; she does not trust the dry cleaner with the embroidered ones.
- **Scent:** cardamom, fried onion, attar (a sandalwood-based blend she has used for years), the laundry soap she prefers. The kitchen scent on her clothing is constant and is one of the things the children describe missing in the bereavement material.

---

## 8. RITUALS, BOTH RELIGIOUS AND IDIOSYNCRATIC

The **five prayers** are the spine. Around them she has constructed personal observances that are not mandated but never skipped:

- A short **morning dua** said standing at the kitchen window, looking at the small backyard, before anyone else is up.
- The **bismillah** before any cooking task of consequence — said audibly when alone, almost inaudibly when others are present.
- The **ayat al-kursi** recited under her breath when anyone leaves the house — especially Kamala, particularly post-revelation, when this recitation lengthens.
- A specific phone-call **dua exchange** with Yusuf when he leaves on any journey longer than the daily commute.
- A **Thursday-night Surah Yaseen** recitation, sometimes attended by other women.
- A **once-a-month** sadaqa (charity) — small cash, given in person where possible, to specific recipients she has identified and tracks privately.

**Idiosyncratic, non-religious rituals** the file would note:

- Reorganizing the spice shelf when she is anxious. The shelf does not need reorganizing; the act calms her.
- **Tea twice a day** minimum, at 7:30 a.m. and 5:00 p.m., with rare deviation. A missed afternoon chai is a stress indicator.
- A particular way of folding fitted sheets that she has tried and failed to teach Kamala for over a decade.
- The Tupperware-distribution ritual after any family meal — leftovers portioned out, labeled implicitly by who is supposed to take what, refused by the recipients only at peril.
